## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the core problem in population dynamics. The relationship captures how birth rates, death rates, and carrying capacity interact to determine population change.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (minimum viable population threshold)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 + P) (reduced growth at low density without extinction threshold)
- Linear density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (quadratic population model)
- Cubic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Harvesting model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (logistic with proportional harvesting)
- Time-varying growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Seasonal modulation: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (periodic environmental forcing)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized growth with asymmetry parameter)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (allometric growth minus mortality)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (density-dependent birth with linear death)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density dependence → Terms with P² or higher powers of P indicate intraspecific competition or cooperation
- Allee effects → Cubic terms in P (or products of two factors involving P) indicate critical population thresholds below which growth becomes negative
- Carrying capacity structure → Factor of form (1 - P/K) or equivalently (1 - c*P) indicates resource limitation with a stable equilibrium
- Logarithmic growth regulation → log(K/P) terms indicate Gompertz-type growth where relative growth rate decreases logarithmically with population
- Time-dependent coefficients → Multiplicative functions of t (exponential, sinusoidal) on growth terms indicate changing environmental conditions or seasonality
- Ratio-dependent terms → P/(1 + c*P) structures indicate saturating functional responses in birth or death processes
- Allometric scaling → Fractional powers P**c with 0<c<1 indicate metabolic or surface-area scaling effects on growth
- Multiple equilibria → Polynomial expressions in P with degree ≥ 3 can produce bistability (e.g., Allee effect models with both extinction and carrying capacity as stable states)

GT: c0*(c1 - exp(-c2*P))*P + c3*P*exp(-c4*t)
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `0.11781609251252895*(1 - exp(-0.027228491244958825*P))*P + 0.11781609251252895*P*exp(-0.027228491244958825*t)`

Let me expand this:
`0.11781609251252895*P - 0.11781609251252895*P*exp(-0.027228491244958825*P) + 0.11781609251252895*P*exp(-0.027228491244958825*t)`

So the GT has three terms:
1. A term proportional to P
2. A term proportional to -P*exp(-αP)
3. A term proportional to P*exp(-βt)

The key structural features are:
- **P*exp(-αP)**: This is a P times an exponential in P
- **P*exp(-βt)**: This is a P times an exponential in t
- **P**: A linear term in P

Now let me check candidates. Most candidates use `tanh` for the P-dependence and various functions for the t-dependence. The `tanh` function cannot exactly reproduce `exp(-αP)` for all P, so the P-dependent part needs careful analysis.

However, `tanh(x) = (1 - exp(-2x))/(1 + exp(-2x))`, which is NOT the same as `1 - exp(-αP)`. The GT has `(1 - exp(-αP))` which is fundamentally different from `tanh`.

Let me focus on candidates with `exp` terms in both P and t:

**Candidate 41:** `P*c0 + P*c1*(c2 + t)**c3 + P*tanh(P*c4 + c5) + c6*exp(P*c7) + c8*exp(c9*t)`

This has `c6*exp(P*c7)` but not `P*exp(P*c7)`. The GT needs `P*exp(-αP)`, not just `exp(-αP)`.

**Candidate 27:** `P*c0 + P*c1*tanh(P*c2 + c3) + P*c4/(c5*t + c6) + c7*exp(P*c8) + c9`

Same issue - `exp(P*c8)` without the P multiplier.

**Candidate 1:** `P*c0 + P*c1*tanh(P*c2 + c3) + P**c4*c5 + c6*exp(c7*t)`

This has `c6*exp(c7*t)` but not `P*exp(c7*t)`. The GT needs P*exp(-βt).

**Candidate 50:** `P*c0 + P*tanh(P*c1 + c2) + P/sqrt(c3 + t) + P**c4*c5 + c6*exp(c7*t)`

Again `c6*exp(c7*t)` not `P*exp(c7*t)`.

None of the candidates have both `P*exp(something in P)` and `P*exp(something in t)` terms simultaneously. The candidates use `tanh` for P-dependence which cannot exactly match `exp(-αP)`, and most use rational functions or power laws for t-dependence rather than `exp(-βt)`.

Let me look more carefully at candidates with `exp(c*t)` multiplied by P... None of them have `P*exp(c*t)` - they all have just `c*exp(c*t)`.

Even candidates 32, 34, 39, 41, 42, 43, 44 which have `exp(c*t)` terms don't multiply them by P.

The GT requires `P*exp(-βt)` as a term. No candidate has a term of the form `P*exp(c*t)`. Therefore, none can match.

Could rational forms like `P*c4/(c5*t + c6)` match `P*exp(-βt)`? No, rational functions cannot equal exponentials for all t.

After careful analysis, no candidate can reproduce both the `P*exp(-αP)` and `P*exp(-βt)` terms of the GT simultaneously. The tanh function cannot replicate exp(-αP), and none of the candidates have `P*exp(c*t)` as a structural term.
